<div id="review_1775731443" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1775731443" />
    <a title="Kaitlyn Ennis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38631186-kaitlyn-ennis"><img alt="Kaitlyn Ennis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567362498p2/38631186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1775731443?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlyn Ennis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlyn Ennis" href="/user/show/38631186-kaitlyn-ennis">Kaitlyn Ennis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30002998-two-by-two">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1775731443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9113412117049341330">This is a difficult review to write. I've been a lifelong fan of Mr. Sparks and have actually read every single one of his books. While they definitely aren't my favorite reads of all time, I have come to appreciate his work for what it is-- a simple, basic and lovely story. However, there are things about this book that I just can't look past. <br/><br/>It's his longest book, and yet the book that didn't need to be even half as long. While I ended up liking Russ and London in the end, the entire first ha</span>
  <span id="freeText9113412117049341330" style="display:none">This is a difficult review to write. I've been a lifelong fan of Mr. Sparks and have actually read every single one of his books. While they definitely aren't my favorite reads of all time, I have come to appreciate his work for what it is-- a simple, basic and lovely story. However, there are things about this book that I just can't look past. <br /><br />It's his longest book, and yet the book that didn't need to be even half as long. While I ended up liking Russ and London in the end, the entire first half was literally their same routine over and over again, and they were so boring, that I had no interest in picking up the book to keep reading. Russ was so bland, without much of a personality and Vivian was so horrible, that I had a very difficult time believing that they were ever in love and the circumstances surrounding the beginnings of their relationship. While some say she was redeemed by the end of the novel, I don't agree. She was so horrible, and Russ just continued to let her be horrible, that I was clutching the book in frustration. While that may have been Sparks' goal, it just didn't work for creating an interesting and captivating story.<br /><br />Marge and Liz were definitely a high point. Their relationship was a first for a Sparks novel, and it was a wonderful breath of fresh air, and reminded me why I've always loved Nicholas Sparks. I wish this novel had been about them. And of course that ending...ugh.<br /><br />Overall, not a huge fan of this one. I can see why people still love it, because it had that beautiful, wrapped-up-in-a-bow ending that Sparks is known for, but that wasn't enough for me to redeem the horribly slow pacing, and unnecessary and excessive plot fillers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9113412117049341330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1783696802" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1783696802" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15754959-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604874267p2/15754959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1783696802?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/15754959-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781455520695" href="/book/show/30002987-two-by-two">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1783696802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6685198643210133405">As a huge Nicholas Sparks fan I always expect a beautiful love story from each of his books. Although not what I was expecting and definitely far from what I've come to expect from his books I have to admit the book was great. Not a lot of dialogue, but that's to be expected as the book is about Russ and London his young daughter. He takes us through their everyday routines while having us go through the emotions Russ is dealing with regarding his failed marriage, his new business, his feelings </span>
  <span id="freeText6685198643210133405" style="display:none">As a huge Nicholas Sparks fan I always expect a beautiful love story from each of his books. Although not what I was expecting and definitely far from what I've come to expect from his books I have to admit the book was great. Not a lot of dialogue, but that's to be expected as the book is about Russ and London his young daughter. He takes us through their everyday routines while having us go through the emotions Russ is dealing with regarding his failed marriage, his new business, his feelings for Emily and then for his sister Marge. <br />I personally related to this book on many levels. I've been where the character of Russ is and know that when a marriage fails no matter the reason why it's devastating. I've had feelings for someone and didn't know what to do about them and know how it can make you feel to not know what to do. Above all else I relate to his character because I know what it's like to watch a loved one battle cancer and watch as they deteriorate slowly and know that their time is coming and being helpless to stop the inevitable. <br />The story is beautifully told and at least for me it's relatable. It is not the usual love story we've come to know and love from Mr. Sparks but it's definitely worth reading. He definitely works wonders and brought tears to my eyes with this beautifully told story about a man whose dealing with so many emotions and attempting to make the best of it while trying to hold himself together to be nothing less than a great father.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6685198643210133405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1620699220" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1620699220" />
    <a title="Christina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14066678-christina"><img alt="Christina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481826762p2/14066678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1620699220?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/14066678-christina">Christina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781455520688" href="/book/show/33296558-two-by-two">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1620699220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3693590952966736102">3.5 stars, rounded up because the characters really stayed with me, even days after I finished this.<br/><br/>32 year old Russ Green seems to have the picture perfect life...a beautiful wife, Vivian, adorable 6 year old daughter, London, a successful career as an advertising executive and a stunning home in Charlotte, close to his mother and father as well as his older sister, Marge and her partner Liz. Anyone looking in would think that he's living the dream. But things aren't always what they seem and u</span>
  <span id="freeText3693590952966736102" style="display:none">3.5 stars, rounded up because the characters really stayed with me, even days after I finished this.<br /><br />32 year old Russ Green seems to have the picture perfect life...a beautiful wife, Vivian, adorable 6 year old daughter, London, a successful career as an advertising executive and a stunning home in Charlotte, close to his mother and father as well as his older sister, Marge and her partner Liz. Anyone looking in would think that he's living the dream. But things aren't always what they seem and underneath the shiny veneer, things are beginning to crumble. In a matter of months, Russ finds himself without a job, without a wife and struggling to raise his daughter alone as he tries to adapt to this new reality that he never had foreseen.<br /><br /><b>"When you start trying to figure out what went wrong - or, more specifically, where <i>you</i> went wrong - it's a bit like peeling an onion. There's always another layer, another mistake in the past or a painful memory that stands out, which then leads one back even further in time, and then even further, in search of the <i>ultimate truth</i>. I've reached the point where I've stopped trying to figure it out. The only thing that really matters now is learning enough to avoid making the same mistakes again."</b><br /><br />This book, like the one just previous to it, See Me had a much different feel when compared to Sparks past novels...not bad necessarily, just different. I ended up putting off reading this for quite some time, and as an avid fan of Sparks, this is unusual when he has a new book. <br />This was about a couple falling apart rather than falling in love and anyone who is familiar with Sparks other novels knows that epic love stories are what he's known for. <br />Now, if I'm being honest, this wasn't my favorite novel of his. But I did enjoy how relatable it was and it was pretty realistic as opposed to some of his past novels where the MC finds their soulmate and declares their love within the span of a few weeks condensed into a few hundred pages. In the end, I was still bawling my eyes out, as I do with nearly all his novels at some point or another...it just wasn't for any reasons I would've really foreseen going into this.<br /><br />Things that frustrated me about this? The main thing would have to be Russ and his lack of backbone when it comes to standing up to Vivian. I was not a fan of hers at all. From the beginning, I didn't really feel any chemistry between them, so I'm not surprised at the path their relationship ultimately took, but Vivian infuriated me along the way and worse was Russ not doing anything about her actions and irrational mood swings, despite being upset by them. He was a people pleaser to the extreme. Not to mention she was a complete hypocrite, selfish and seemingly devoid of any warmth. This novel was done in 1st person POV and thank goodness it was all through Russ. I might've thrown this book across the room if I would've had to read through Vivian's POV.<br />When it came to London, she seemed older, more mature, than a 6 year old to me. Her dialogue was still adorably precious. My favorite character by far was Marge. She was witty, snarky and brave throughout many points in the story (her story's ending has me shaking my fist at you Sparks!) <br />As far as Emily goes...an Ex of Russ and the ultimate 'new ' love interest once Vivian's out of the picture. I'm torn...I liked her character and I liked that she provided more in the way of friendship than romantic love to Russ, but I honestly think the story would've been ok had she just remained a platonic friend. It almost seemed like the book was going to veer in the direction of their great love story and the conflict would be Vivian's reaction to it, maybe even resulting in an awkward love triangle, but luckily that wasn't the case.<br /><br />What I would love to see come from this? I would've really enjoyed getting a better insight into Liz...I think her storyline wasn't explored as well as it could've been...especially considering how long this book was. It would be so great to see her get her own novel down the line, touching on how she's doing after everything and what direction her life takes (hinted at very lightly in the end, but I want more!). I would be all over that!<br /><br />All in all, if you're looking for a tender, epic romance reminiscent of Spark's past tearjerkers, don't expect it from this novel. You'll enjoy it more if you don't go into this expecting that kind of story... If you're looking for a realistic portrait of a man trying to pick up the pieces of his life after his reality is shattered and his path along the way, then this book could be for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3693590952966736102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Good thing Vivian is a fictional character because I would so go hunt her down and dog slap her! Ugh! HATE. HER. <br/><br/>OK, now that I've got that out of the way, I feel a tiny bit better. This book is so good! Really! It's fiction but it's not. It's incredibly realistic and very believable. It's NOT a romance book though. If you are looking for a love story, this book is not for you. But if you're looking for a great book about a fat</span>
  <span id="freeText2304322885976743824" style="display:none">I hate that heifer with a passion I cannot express with words alone. <div id="review_1676640592" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1676640592" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/110328-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601905208p2/110328.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1676640592?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/110328-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30002998-two-by-two">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1676640592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5754673332918453090">I’ve been a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2345.Nicholas_Sparks' title='Nicholas Sparks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nicholas Sparks</a> fan since the late ‘90s, so I was excited to read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30002998.Two_By_Two' title='Two By Two by Nicholas Sparks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Two By Two</a> as soon as I could get my hands on it. Compared to his high intensity novels, such as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7812659.Safe_Haven' title='Safe Haven by Nicholas Sparks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Safe Haven</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24820165.See_Me' title='See Me by Nicholas Sparks' rel='nofollow noopener'>See Me</a>, this one is more subdued. There are some heavy and sad moments, but there’s a balance of joy and romance, as well. He addresses the family dynamic from the man’s perspective and explores the things that can go awry when trying to find balance. <br/> <br/>Russ suddenly finds himself in the role of “Mr. Mom” (rem</span>
  <span id="freeText5754673332918453090" style="display:none">I’ve been a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2345.Nicholas_Sparks" title="Nicholas Sparks" rel="nofollow noopener">Nicholas Sparks</a> fan since the late ‘90s, so I was excited to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30002998.Two_By_Two" title="Two By Two by Nicholas Sparks" rel="nofollow noopener">Two By Two</a> as soon as I could get my hands on it. Compared to his high intensity novels, such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7812659.Safe_Haven" title="Safe Haven by Nicholas Sparks" rel="nofollow noopener">Safe Haven</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24820165.See_Me" title="See Me by Nicholas Sparks" rel="nofollow noopener">See Me</a>, this one is more subdued. There are some heavy and sad moments, but there’s a balance of joy and romance, as well. He addresses the family dynamic from the man’s perspective and explores the things that can go awry when trying to find balance. <br /> <br />Russ suddenly finds himself in the role of “Mr. Mom” (remember the Lonestar song?) after some mishaps at his job that lead him to make a drastic change in his career plan. This soon leads to tension with his wife and trying to find a new balance between caring for his daughter and his future aspirations. <br /> <br />The story starts out a bit slow, but then picks up steam when the climax is reached. After that, there are moments when it stagnates and other times when it races ahead. I enjoyed reading about Russ’ relationship with his daughter, parents, and sister. I didn’t so much enjoy reading the parts involving his wife, but mostly because she seemed like a complete shrew. She ran hot and cold and was extremely manipulative and bossy. It made me wonder what was going on behind the scenes to inspire such a character. However, she kept me guessing as to where things would go in the story, since a lot of the drama tended to ride on her personality shifts. <br /> <br />While I was surprised at one outcome, there were other parts that were predictable. The story wrapped up a bit too neatly, even though I was glad to receive some closure from the situation at hand. One aspect was really sad, but I felt prepared for it in some ways. It didn't make me cry, but I'm sure I'd be a sobbing mess if I saw it in a movie version. (That happened with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6400090.The_Last_Song" title="The Last Song by Nicholas Sparks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Song</a>.)<br /> <br />In addition, I liked that there was a lesbian couple featured in the story. Especially since Nicholas portrayed them as having a more positive and loving relationship than the straight couple that was the main focus of the story. I hope more novels will continue on this trend, including featuring a lesbian or gay couple as the main characters.<br /> <br />Overall, <i>Two by Two</i> was a sweet story about family and love and there are some good messages that came out of it. <br /> <br />Since I’m sure this will become a movie (as most of his books do), here are my casting choices. You’re welcome, Hollywood.<br />Russ: <a href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm1475594/?ref_=nv_sr_1" rel="nofollow noopener">Channing Tatum</a> (I know he was in Dear John, but he’s just so right for this role)<br />Vivian: <a href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm0305272/" rel="nofollow noopener">JoAnna Garcia Swisher</a><br />Emily: <a href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm0162233/?ref_=nv_sr_1" rel="nofollow noopener">Natalia Cigliuti </a>(I recently saw her on an episode of This is Us and she just seemed like a perfect fit)<br />Marge: <a href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm0005513/" rel="nofollow noopener">Alanna Ubach</a><br />Liz: <a href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm1128572/" rel="nofollow noopener">Lake Bell</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5754673332918453090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('K3BqIW+5QQCOTA3K5yTmXYHZL8vxbLt1ZIkb2IRj/i+dZLKc0D0QkNyLL+xJam6Yd9pZ1j8zWBt2w6MYAW3Gjw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ko4oMa25II8P+wfgOalJNcyCnLykILua54Q8zCU/7m4kmvCMEj1xH108JcaX58HwOoHqoWp/WPT1zoQMoDHWzg==')})
  }

//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_39072210'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39072210-a-spark-of-light?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">A Spark of Light<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/7128.Jodi_Picoult?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Jodi Picoult<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.70 avg rating &mdash; 98,981 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2018\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer5691566264025728113\">The warm fall day starts like any other at the Center—a women’s reproductive health services clinic—its staff offering care to anyone who passes through its doors. Then, in late morning, a desperate and distraught gunman bursts in and opens fire, tak<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText5691566264025728113\" style=\"display:none\">The warm fall day starts like any other at the Center—a women’s reproductive health services clinic—its staff offering care to anyone who passes through its doors. Then, in late morning, a desperate and distraught gunman bursts in and opens fire, taking all inside hostage.\n\nAfter rushing to the scene, Hugh McElroy, a police hostage negotiator, sets up a perimeter and begins making a plan to communicate with the gunman. As his phone vibrates with incoming text messages he glances at it and, to his horror, finds out that his fifteen-year-old daughter, Wren, is inside the clinic.\n\nBut Wren is not alone. She will share the next and tensest few hours of her young life with a cast of unforgettable characters: A nurse who calms her own panic in order save the life of a wounded woman. A doctor who does his work not in spite of his faith but because of it, and who will find that faith tested as never before. A pro-life protester disguised as a patient, who now stands in the cross hairs of the same rage she herself has felt. A young woman who has come to terminate her pregnancy. And the disturbed individual himself, vowing to be heard.\n\nTold in a daring and enthralling narrative structure that counts backward through the hours of the standoff, this is a story that traces its way back to what brought each of these very different individuals to the same place on this fateful day.\n\nJodi Picoult—one of the most fearless writers of our time—tackles a complicated issue in this gripping and nuanced novel.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2345.Nicholas_Sparks">About Nicholas Sparks</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2345.Nicholas_Sparks"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1591799426p3/2345.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/2345.Nicholas_Sparks">Nicholas Sparks
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3855204303096577648">Nicholas Sparks is one of the world’s most beloved storytellers. All of his books have been <i>New York Times</i> bestsellers, with over 105 million copies sold worldwide, in more than 50 languages, including over 75 million copies in the United States alone.<br/><br/>Sparks wrote one of his best-known stories, <i>The Notebook</i>, over a period of six months at age 28. It was published in 1996 and he followed with the n</span>
  <span id="freeText3855204303096577648" style="display:none">Nicholas Sparks is one of the world’s most beloved storytellers. All of his books have been <i>New York Times</i> bestsellers, with over 105 million copies sold worldwide, in more than 50 languages, including over 75 million copies in the United States alone.<br /><br />Sparks wrote one of his best-known stories, <i>The Notebook</i>, over a period of six months at age 28. It was published in 1996 and he followed with the novels <i>Message in a Bottle</i> (1998), <i>A Walk to Remember</i> (1999), <i>The Rescue</i> (2000), <i>A Bend in the Road</i> (2001), <i>Nights in Rodanthe</i> (2002), <i>The Guardian</i> (2003), <i>The Wedding</i> (2003), <i>True Believer</i> (2005) and its sequel, <i>At First Sight</i> (2005), <i>Dear John</i> (2006), <i>The Choice</i> (2007), <i>The Lucky One</i> (2008), <i>The Last Song</i> (2009), <i>Safe Haven</i> (2010), <i>The Best of Me</i> (2011), <i>The Longest Ride</i> (2013), <i>See Me</i> (2015), <i>Two by Two</i> (2016) and Every Breath (2018) as well as the 2004 non-fiction memoir <i>Three Weeks With My Brother</i>, co-written with his brother Micah. His twenty-first novel, <i>The Return</i>, will be published on September 29, 2020.<br /><br />Film adaptations of Nicholas Sparks novels, including <i>The Choice</i>, <i>The Longest Ride</i>, <i>The Best of Me</i>, <i>Safe Haven</i> (on all of which he served as a producer), <i>The Lucky One</i>, <i>Message in a Bottle</i>, <i>A Walk to Remember</i>,<i> The Notebook</i>, <i>Nights in Rodanthe</i>, <i>Dear John</i> and <i>The Last Song</i>, have had a cumulative worldwide gross of over three-quarters of a billion dollars. <i> The Notebook</i> is also being adapted into a musical, featuring music and lyrics by Ingrid Michaelson. <br /><br />Sparks lives in North Carolina. He contributes to a variety of local and national charities, and is a major contributor to the Creative Writing Program (MFA) at the University of Notre Dame, where he provides scholarships, internships, and a fellowship annually. He co-founded The Epiphany School in New Bern, North Carolina in 2006. As a former full scholarship athlete (he still holds a track and field record at the University of Notre Dame) he also spent four years coaching track and field athletes at the local public high school. In 2009, the team he coached at New Bern High School set a World Junior Indoor Record in the 4x400 meter, in New York. The record still stands. <br /><br />The Nicholas Sparks Foundation, a 501(c)(3) nonprofit committed to improving cultural and international understanding through global education experiences for students of all ages was launched in 2011. Between the foundation, and the personal gifts of the Sparks family, more than $15 million dollars have been distributed to deserving charities, scholarship programs, and projects. Because the Sparks family covers all operational expenses of the foundation, 100% of donations are devoted to programs.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3855204303096577648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
